## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph Code Search Tools BEFORE Any Code Changes

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available (keyword_search, nls_search, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read). You MUST use them as your primary code discovery method.

Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide.

# big-code-camel-arch-001: Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture

## Task

Trace how Apache Camel routes a message from endpoint reception through the EIP pipeline to a destination. Map the complete Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer hierarchy, including the Pipeline processor chain, Channel interceptor wiring, and the RouteReifier model-to-runtime bridge.

## Context

- **Repository**: apache/camel (Java, ~2.8M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: core/ — the Camel core routing engine (camel-api, camel-support, camel-core-processor, camel-base-engine, camel-core-reifier)

## Requirements

1. Identify all relevant components in the Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer hierarchy (API interfaces + base implementations)
2. Trace the dependency chain from route definition through reification to runtime message processing
3. Document the Pipeline and Channel architecture (how processors are chained and intercepted)
4. Explain how the RouteReifier bridges the DSL model (RouteDefinition) to the runtime Route

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

package org.apache.camel;

/**
 * A <a href="http://camel.apache.org/processor.html">processor</a> is used to implement the
 * <a href="http://camel.apache.org/event-driven-consumer.html"> Event Driven Consumer</a> and
 * <a href="http://camel.apache.org/message-translator.html"> Message Translator</a> patterns and to process message
 * exchanges.
 * <p/>
 * Notice if you use a {@link Processor} in a Camel route, then make sure to write the {@link Processor} in a
 * thread-safe way, as the Camel routes can potentially be executed by concurrent threads, and therefore multiple
 * threads can call the same {@link Processor} instance.
 */
@FunctionalInterface
public interface Processor {

    /**
     * Processes the message exchange
     *
     * @param  exchange  the message exchange
     * @throws Exception if an internal processing error has occurred.
     */
    void process(Exchange exchange) throws Exception;
}

101-usertool_resultTask
Perfect! I've found all the key classes in the Apache Camel core routing engine. Here's a comprehensive summary with full file paths:

## Key Classes in Apache Camel Core Routing Engine

### 1. **Pipeline** - Processor that chains processors in sequence
**Path:** `/workspace/core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/Pipeline.java`

**Role:** Creates a Pipeline pattern where the output of the previous step is sent as input to the next step, reusing the same message exchanges. Implements `Navigate<Processor>`, `Traceable`, and manages a list of `AsyncProcessor` instances that are executed sequentially through an internal `PipelineTask` that implements `PooledExchangeTask`.

---

### 2. **CamelInternalProcessor** - Internal processor with cross-cutting concerns
**Path:** `/workspace/core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java`

**Role:** Internal processor that the Camel routing engine uses during routing for cross-cutting functionality including:
- Execute Unit of Work
- Track which route is currently being routed
- Execute Route Policy
- Gather JMX performance statistics
- Tracing, Debugging, Message History
- Stream Caching, Transformers
- And more infrastructure concerns

---

### 3. **Channel** - Interface that wraps processors with interceptors
**Path:** `/workspace/core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Channel.java`

**Role:** Acts as a channel between processors in the route graph. Extends `AsyncProcessor` and `Navigate<Processor>`. Responsible for:
- Initializing channels with route information, definitions, interceptors
- Wrapping output with interceptors and error handlers
- Providing access to the next processor and error handler
- Managing the route context

---

## Summary: Core Routing Hierarchy in Apache Camel

Here are the base/support implementations for the core routing hierarchy in the Apache Camel project:

### 1. **DefaultComponent**
**File Path:** `/workspace/core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultComponent.java`

**Key Methods:**
- `createEndpoint(String uri, Map<String, Object> properties)` - Main factory method for creating endpoints, handles URI parsing, parameter validation, and endpoint configuration
- `createEndpoint(String uri)` - Convenience overload
- `createEndpoint(String uri, String remaining, Map<String, Object> parameters)` - Abstract method for subclasses to implement endpoint creation
- `setProperties(Endpoint endpoint, Map<String, Object> parameters)` - Configures endpoint using parameters
- `setProperties(Object bean, Map<String, Object> parameters)` - Generic property setting for any bean
- `afterConfiguration(String uri, String remaining, Endpoint endpoint, Map<String, Object> parameters)` - Post-configuration hook
- `validateURI(String uri, String path, Map<String, Object> parameters)` - URI validation strategy
- `validateParameters(String uri, Map<String, Object> parameters, String optionPrefix)` - Parameter validation
- `getComponentPropertyConfigurer()` - Returns property configurer for component
- `getEndpointPropertyConfigurer()` - Returns property configurer for endpoints

**Key Properties:**
- `autowiredEnabled` - Enables automatic autowiring of options
- `bridgeErrorHandler` - Bridges consumer to Camel routing Error Handler
- `lazyStartProducer` - Defers producer startup until first message

    public abstract Processor createProcessor() throws Exception;

    /**
     * Prefer to use {#link #createChildProcessor}.
     */
    protected Processor createOutputsProcessor() throws Exception {
        Collection<ProcessorDefinition<?>> outputs = definition.getOutputs();
        return createOutputsProcessor(outputs);
    }

    /**
     * Creates the child processor (outputs) from the current definition
     *
     * @param  mandatory whether or not children is mandatory (ie the definition should have outputs)
     * @return           the created children, or <tt>null</tt> if definition had no output
     * @throws Exception is thrown if error creating the child or if it was mandatory and there was no output defined on
     *                   definition
     */
    protected Processor createChildProcessor(boolean mandatory) throws Exception {
        Processor children = null;
        // at first use custom factory
        final ProcessorFactory processorFactory = PluginHelper.getProcessorFactory(camelContext);
        if (processorFactory != null) {
            children = processorFactory.createChildProcessor(route,
                    definition, mandatory);
        }
        // fallback to default implementation if factory did not create the
        // child
        if (children == null) {
            children = createOutputsProcessor();
        }

        if (children == null && mandatory) {
            throw new IllegalArgumentException("Definition has no children on " + definition);
        }
        return children;
    }

        if (processor == null) {
            // no processor to add
            return;
        }

    @Override
    public boolean process(Exchange exchange, AsyncCallback originalCallback) {
        // ----------------------------------------------------------
        // CAMEL END USER - READ ME FOR DEBUGGING TIPS
        // ----------------------------------------------------------
        // If you want to debug the Camel routing engine, then there is a lot of internal functionality
        // the routing engine executes during routing messages. You can skip debugging this internal
        // functionality and instead debug where the routing engine continues routing to the next node
        // in the routes. The CamelInternalProcessor is a vital part of the routing engine, as its
        // being used in between the nodes. As an end user you can just debug the code in this class
        // in between the:
        //   CAMEL END USER - DEBUG ME HERE +++ START +++
        //   CAMEL END USER - DEBUG ME HERE +++ END +++
        // you can see in the code below within the processTransacted or processNonTransacted methods.
        // ----------------------------------------------------------

        if (processor == null || exchange.isRouteStop()) {
            // no processor or we should not continue then we are done
            originalCallback.done(true);
            return true;
        }
        if (this instanceof Channel ca && ca.getNextProcessor() instanceof DisabledAware da && da.isDisabled()) {

    @Override
    public boolean process(Exchange exchange, final AsyncCallback callback) {
        if (!isStarted()) {
            exchange.setException(new IllegalStateException("SendProcessor has not been started: " + this));
            callback.done(true);
            return true;
        }

        // we should preserve existing MEP so remember old MEP
        // if you want to permanently to change the MEP then use .setExchangePattern in the DSL
        final ExchangePattern existingPattern = exchange.getPattern();

        // when using variables then we need to remember original data
        Object body = null;
        Map<String, Object> headers = null;
        if (variableSend != null || variableReceive != null) {
            try {
                body = exchange.getMessage().getBody();
                // do a defensive copy of the headers
                headers = headersMapFactory.newMap(exchange.getMessage().getHeaders());
            } catch (Exception throwable) {
                exchange.setException(throwable);
                callback.done(true);
                return true;
            }
        }
        final Object originalBody = body;
        final Map<String, Object> originalHeaders = headers;

        if (extendedStatistics) {
            counter.incrementAndGet();
        }

        // if we have a producer then use that as its optimized
        if (producer != null) {
            return sendUsingProducer(exchange, callback, existingPattern, originalBody, originalHeaders);
        } else {
            // we can send with a different MEP pattern
            return sendUsingPattern(exchange, callback, existingPattern, originalBody, originalHeaders);
        }
    }

    private boolean sendUsingPattern(

    @Override
    @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
    public Navigate<Processor> navigate() {
        Processor answer = getProcessor();

        // we want to navigate routes to be easy, so skip the initial channel
        // and navigate to its output where it all starts from end user point of view
        if (answer instanceof Navigate nav) {
            if (nav.next().size() == 1) {
                Object first = nav.next().get(0);
                if (first instanceof Navigate) {
                    return (Navigate<Processor>) first;
                }
            }
            return (Navigate<Processor>) answer;
        }
        return null;
    }

    @Override
    public List<Processor> filter(String pattern) {
        List<Processor> match = new ArrayList<>();
        doFilter(pattern.split(","), navigate(), match);
        return match;
    }

    /**
     * Factory method to lazily create the complete list of services required for this route such as adding the
     * processor or consumer
     */
    protected void gatherServices(List<Service> services) throws Exception {
        // first gather the root services
        gatherRootServices(services);
        // and then all the child services
        List<Service> children = new ArrayList<>();
        for (Service service : services) {
            Set<Service> extra = ServiceHelper.getChildServices(service);
            children.addAll(extra);
        }
        for (Service extra : children) {
            if (!services.contains(extra)) {
                services.add(extra);
            }
        }
    }

    private void gatherRootServices(List<Service> services) throws Exception {

                resumeStrategy.setAdapter(resumeAdapter);
                resumeAware.setResumeStrategy(

190-assistanttext-
The analysis has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here's a brief overview of what was traced:

**Core Hierarchy**: `Component` (factory) → `Endpoint` (factory) → `Consumer`/`Producer`, with `Processor` as the universal processing contract. All API interfaces live in `core/camel-api/`, with base implementations in `core/camel-support/`.

**Reification Bridge**: `RouteReifier` converts the design-time `RouteDefinition` model into a runtime `Route` by:
1. Resolving the input endpoint from `FromDefinition`
2. Iterating each output `ProcessorDefinition`, delegating to the matching `ProcessorReifier` (e.g., `SendReifier` for `to()`)
3. Each reifier creates a `Processor`, which gets wrapped in a `DefaultChannel` with interceptors and error handlers
4. All channels are assembled into a `RoutePipeline`, wrapped in a `CamelInternalProcessor` with UoW/policy/JMX advices

**Pipeline + Channel Architecture**: `Pipeline` chains processors sequentially using a `PipelineTask` scheduled on the `ReactiveExecutor`. `DefaultChannel` extends `CamelInternalProcessor` to add per-node cross-cutting concerns (tracing, debugging, message history, JMX) via the `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice` before/after pattern. The terminal `SendProcessor` resolves a destination `Producer` and delivers the exchange.

encodedUri = UnsafeUriCharactersEncoder.encode(uri);\n        URI u = new URI(encodedUri);\n        String path;\n        if (u.getScheme() != null) {\n            // if there is a scheme then there is also a path\n            path = URISupport.extractRemainderPath(u, useRawUri());\n        } else {\n            // this uri has no context-path as the leading text is the component name (scheme)\n            path = null;\n        }\n\n        // use encoded or raw uri?\n        Map<String, Object> parameters;\n        if (useRawUri()) {\n            // when using raw uri then the query is taking    }\n\n        @Override\n        public void prepare(Exchange exchange, AsyncCallback callback) {\n            this.exchange = exchange;\n            this.callback = callback;\n continueProcessing(exchange, \"so breaking out of pipeline\", LOG))) {\n\n                // prepare for next run\n                ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn(exchange);\n\n                // get the next processor\n                AsyncProcessor processor = processors.get(index++);\n\n                processor.process(exchange, this);\n            } else {\n                // copyResults is needed in case MEP is OUT and the message is not an OUT message\n                ExchangeHelper.copyResults(exchange, exchange);\n\n                // logging nextExchange as it contains the exchange that might have altered the payload and since\n                // we are logging the completion it will be confusing if we log the original instead\n                // we could also consider logging the original and the nextExchange then we have *before* and *after* snapshots\n                if (LOG.isTraceEnabled()) {\n                    LOG.trace(\"Processing complete for exchangeId: {} >>> {}\", exchange.getExchangeId(), exchange);\n                }\n\n                AsyncCallback cb = callback;\n                taskFactory.release(this);\n                reactiveExecutor.schedule(cb);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    public Pipeline(CamelContext camelContext, Collection<Processor> processors) {\n        this.camelContext = camelContext;\n processors) {\n            if (processor != null) {\n                toBeProcessed.add(processor);\n            }\n        }\n\n        return new Pipeline(camelContext, toBeProcessed);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean process(Exchange exchange, AsyncCallback callback) {\n        try {\n            // create task which has state used during routing\n            PooledExchangeTask task = reactiveExecutor.scheduleMain(task);\n            }\n            return false;\n        } catch (Exception e) {\n            exchange.setException(e);\n            callback.done(true);\n It's still an exception, the exchange still failed.\n            if (log.isDebugEnabled()) {\n                StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(256);\n                sb.append(\"Message exchange has failed: \").append(message).append(\" for exchange: \").append(exchange);\n                if (exchange.isRollbackOnly() || exchange.isRollbackOnlyLast()) {\n                    sb.append(\" Marked as rollback only.\");\n                }\n                if (exchange.getException() != null) {\n                    sb.append(\" Exception: \").append(exchange.getException());\n                }\n                if (exchange.getExchangeExtension().isErrorHandlerHandledSet()\n                        && exchange.getExchangeExtension().isErrorHandlerHandled()) {\n                    sb.append(\" Handled by the error handler.\");\n                }\n                log.debug(sb.toString());\n            }\n\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        // check for stop\n        if (exchange.isRouteStop()) {\n            if (log.isDebugEnabled()) {\n                log.debug(\"ExchangeId: {} is marked to stop routing: {}\", exchange.getExchangeId(), exchange);\n            }\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        return true;\n    }\n\n}"

  "content": "# Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### API Interfaces (core/camel-api)\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Component.java` \u2014 Factory interface for creating Endpoint instances from URIs; extends CamelContextAware, Service\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Endpoint.java` \u2014 Message Endpoint pattern interface; factory for Producer, Consumer, and Exchange instances\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Consumer.java` \u2014 Consumes message exchanges from an Endpoint; holds a reference to the processing Processor\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Producer.java` \u2014 Sends message exchanges to an Endpoint; extends both Processor and Service\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Processor.java` \u2014 Core @FunctionalInterface for processing Exchange instances; single method `process(Exchange)`\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Channel.java` \u2014 Routes exchanges between processors in the route graph; wraps processors with interceptors and error handlers\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Route.java` \u2014 Runtime route interface defining lifecycle, configuration, policies, and consumer/processor access\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/spi/InternalProcessor.java` \u2014 Internal processor API for cross-cutting concerns (UoW, tracing, debugging, JMX, route policies)\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/spi/CamelInternalProcessorAdvice.java` \u2014 Before/after advice interface for cross-cutting functionality in the routing engine\n\n### Base/Support Implementations (core/camel-support)\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultComponent.java` \u2014 Abstract base Component; implements URI parsing, parameter extraction, endpoint creation/configuration lifecycle\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultEndpoint.java` \u2014 Abstract base Endpoint; manages exchange creation, consumer/producer factory methods, polling consumer setup\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultConsumer.java` \u2014 Default Consumer implementation; manages UnitOfWork lifecycle, exchange factory, async processor delegation, exception handling\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultProducer.java` \u2014 Abstract base Producer; delegates exchange creation to endpoint\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultAsyncProducer.java` \u2014 Async-capable Producer; bridges sync process() to async via AsyncProcessorAwaitManager\n\n### Processor Chain (core/camel-core-processor)\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/Pipeline.java` \u2014 Chains processors sequentially; output of one becomes input to the next via PipelineTask/ReactiveExecutor\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/RoutePipeline.java` \u2014 Subclass of Pipeline used as the starting point for a Route\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/PipelineHelper.java` \u2014 Decides whether to continue processing based on exchange failure/rollback/stop state\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/SendProcessor.java` \u2014 Terminal processor that forwards an exchange to a destination Endpoint via its Producer\n\n### Engine (core/camel-base-engine)\n- `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultRoute.java` \u2014 Default Route implementation; creates Consumer from Endpoint.createConsumer(processor), manages services lifecycle\n- `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultChannel.java` \u2014 Default Channel implementation (extends CamelInternalProcessor); wires interceptors, error handlers, debugger, tracer, and JMX instrumentation around each processor node\n- `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java` \u2014 Core internal processor executing CamelInternalProcessorAdvice before/after callbacks for UoW, route policy, inflight tracking, tracing, debugging, stream caching, message history\n\n### Model (core/camel-core-model)\n- `core/camel-core-model/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/model/RouteDefinition.java` \u2014 DSL model class for a route; holds FromDefinition (input), outputs (processor definitions), error handler, route policies, and configuration\n\n### Reifiers (core/camel-core-reifier)\n- `core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/RouteReifier.java` \u2014 Bridges RouteDefinition model to runtime Route; resolves endpoints, creates RoutePipeline, wraps with CamelInternalProcessor/UoW, configures route policies and advices\n- `core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/ProcessorReifier.java` \u2014 Abstract base reifier; converts ProcessorDefinition to Processor, wraps each in a Channel with interceptors and error handlers, builds composite Pipeline from outputs\n- `core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/SendReifier.java` \u2014 Converts ToDefinition to SendProcessor; resolves the destination Endpoint\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### Phase 1: Route Definition (Design Time / DSL)\n1. Entry point: `core/camel-core-model/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/model/RouteDefinition.java`\n   - User defines a route via Java DSL (`from(\"timer:tick\").to(\"log:out\")`) or XML\n   - `RouteDefinition` holds a `FromDefinition` (input endpoint) and a list of `ProcessorDefinition` outputs (each EIP step)\n\n### Phase 2: Route Reification (Startup / Model\u2192Runtime Bridge)\n2. `RouteReifier.createRoute()` \u2192 `doCreateRoute()`\n   (`core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/RouteReifier.java`)\n   - Resolves the input `Endpoint` from the `FromDefinition`'s URI via `resolveEndpoint()`\n   - Creates a `DefaultRoute` via `PluginHelper.getRouteFactory()` with the resolved endpoint\n   - Configures route-level settings: error handler factory, tracing, message history, stream caching, delayer, auto-startup, shutdown policy\n\n3. For each output `ProcessorDefinition` in `RouteDefinition.getOutputs()`:\n   - `ProcessorReifier.reifier(route, output)` selects the appropriate reifier (e.g., `SendReifier` for `ToDefinition`)\n   - `reifier.addRoutes()` is called, which invokes `makeProcessor()`:\n     a. `createProcessor()` \u2014 calls the specific reifier's implementation (e.g., `SendReifier.createProcessor()` creates a `SendProcessor`)\n     b. `wrapProcessor(processor)` \u2192 `wrapChannel(processor, child)`:\n        - Creates a `DefaultChannel` via `PluginHelper.getInternalProcessorFactory().createChannel()`\n        - Collects interceptor strategies from: CamelContext \u2192 Route \u2192 Definition\n        - Calls `channel.initChannel()` which wires: JMX instrumentation, tracer, debugger, backlog tracer, message history advices\n        - Optionally wraps the channel output in an error handler via `wrapChannelInErrorHandler()`\n        - Calls `channel.postInitChannel()` to finalize wiring\n     c. The wrapped `Channel` is added to `route.getEventDrivenProcessors()`\n\n4. RouteReifier assembles the list of event-driven processors into a `RoutePipeline`\n   (`core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/RoutePipeline.java`)\n\n5. RouteReifier wraps the `RoutePipeline` in a `CamelInternalProcessor` with UnitOfWork advice:\n   - `PluginHelper.getInternalProcessorFactory().addUnitOfWorkProcessorAdvice(camelContext, target, route)`\n   - Adds route policy advice, inflight repository advice, JMX management advice, route lifecycle advice\n   - Adds REST binding advice, contract advice, variable advice as applicable\n   - Sets this `InternalProcessor` as `route.setProcessor(internal)`\n\n### Phase 3: Route Startup (Runtime)\n6. `DefaultRoute.gatherRootServices()` \u2192 `endpoint.createConsumer(processor)`\n   (`core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultRoute.java:685`)\n   - The route's endpoint creates a `Consumer` passing the route's processor (the `CamelInternalProcessor` wrapping the `RoutePipeline`)\n   - The consumer is started as part of the route's service lifecycle\n\n### Phase 4: Message Processing (Runtime)\n7. Consumer receives a message from the external source (e.g., timer fires, HTTP request arrives):\n   - `DefaultConsumer.createExchange(autoRelease)` creates a new `Exchange` from the `ExchangeFactory`\n   - Consumer calls `getAsyncProcessor().process(exchange, callback)` \u2014 this invokes the route's processor chain\n\n8. `CamelInternalProcessor.process(exchange, callback)` (top-level UoW wrapper):\n   (`core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java:285`)\n   - Executes all `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice.before(exchange)` in order:\n     - UnitOfWork creation/tracking\n     - Route policy `onExchangeBegin()`\n     - Inflight repository increment\n     - JMX instrumentation start\n     - Message history recording\n     - Stream caching\n   - Delegates to `processor.process(exchange, asyncCallback)` \u2014 the wrapped `RoutePipeline`\n   - After completion, executes all advices' `after(exchange, state)` in reverse order\n\n9. `Pipeline.process(exchange, callback)` (the RoutePipeline):\n   (`core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/Pipeline.java`)\n   - Acquires a `PipelineTask` from the task factory\n   - Schedules the task on the `ReactiveExecutor`\n   - `PipelineTask.run()` iterates through the processor list:\n     a. Calls `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn(exchange)` to copy OUT\u2192IN for the next step\n     b. Calls `PipelineHelper.continueProcessing(exchange)` to check for errors/stop/rollback\n     c. Gets the next `AsyncProcessor` (which is a `DefaultChannel` wrapping the actual EIP processor)\n     d. Calls `processor.process(exchange, this)` where `this` (PipelineTask) is the callback\n     e. On callback `done()`, re-schedules itself via `ReactiveExecutor` to process the next step\n     f. When all processors are exhausted, calls `ExchangeHelper.copyResults()` and signals the original callback\n\n10. `DefaultChannel.process(exchange, callback)` (each EIP step):\n    (`core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultChannel.java`)\n    - DefaultChannel extends `CamelInternalProcessor`, so it follows the same advice pattern:\n      - Executes per-node advices: message history, debugger, backlog tracer, JMX instrumentation\n      - Delegates to its output \u2014 which is either the error handler wrapping the next processor, or the next processor directly\n    - The error handler intercepts exceptions and applies redelivery/dead-letter-channel policies\n\n11. At a `to(\"...\")` step, the `SendProcessor.process(exchange, callback)` is invoked:\n    (`core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/SendProcessor.java`)\n    - Resolves and caches the destination's `AsyncProducer`\n    - Calls `producer.process(exchange, callback)` to deliver the exchange to the destination endpoint\n    - Restores the original exchange pattern after send\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Abstract Factory Pattern**: `Component` \u2192 `Endpoint` \u2192 `Consumer`/`Producer`. Each Component is a factory for Endpoints, and each Endpoint is a factory for Consumers and Producers. This three-level factory hierarchy enables pluggable transport/protocol support.\n\n2. **Pipes and Filters (Pipeline) Pattern**: The `Pipeline` processor implements the classic Pipes and Filters EIP. Each processor in the pipeline receives the output of the previous processor as its input. The `PipelineTask` manages sequential execution through the processor chain using a reactive callback model.\n\n3. **Chain of Responsibility Pattern**: The `Channel` (DefaultChannel) wraps each processor node with interceptors and error handlers, forming a chain of responsibility. Interceptor strategies are collected from three scopes: CamelContext-global, route-level, and definition-level.\n\n4. **Interceptor / Advice Pattern**: `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice` implements the before/after advice pattern for cross-cutting concerns. Multiple advices are composed into the `CamelInternalProcessor` and executed in sorted order (via `Ordered`), with `after()` callbacks running in reverse order. This replaces what would otherwise be deeply nested processor wrappers, reducing stack depth.\n\n5. **Bridge Pattern (Reifier)**: The `ProcessorReifier` hierarchy bridges the model layer (design-time DSL definitions) to the runtime layer (executable processors). Each `ProcessorDefinition` subclass has a corresponding `ProcessorReifier` that knows how to create the runtime processor. `RouteReifier` orchestrates this for the entire route.\n\n6. **Template Method Pattern**: `DefaultComponent.createEndpoint(String uri)` implements the template method \u2014 it handles URI parsing, parameter extraction, and property binding, then delegates to the abstract `createEndpoint(String uri, String remaining, Map<String, Object> parameters)` which concrete components override.\n\n7. **Decorator Pattern**: The `DefaultChannel` decorates the actual processor with error handling, interceptors, debugging, tracing, and JMX instrumentation. The `CamelInternalProcessor` at the route level decorates the entire `RoutePipeline` with UnitOfWork, route policy, and inflight tracking.\n\n8. **Object Pool Pattern**: Both `Pipeline` and `CamelInternalProcessor` use `PooledExchangeTaskFactory` and `PooledObjectFactory` respectively to reuse task objects, reducing GC pressure in high-throughput scenarios.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|-----------|---------------|\n| `Component` | URI-based factory for Endpoints; handles component-level configuration |\n| `Endpoint` | Factory for Consumers and Producers; defines exchange pattern; provides exchange creation |\n| `Consumer` | Receives messages from external source; creates Exchange; delegates to processor chain |\n| `Producer` | Sends Exchange to external destination; implements Processor interface |\n| `Processor` | Core processing unit; single `process(Exchange)` method |\n| `Pipeline` / `RoutePipeline` | Chains processors sequentially using reactive execution model |\n| `Channel` / `DefaultChannel` | Wraps individual processors with interceptors, error handlers, tracing, debugging |\n| `CamelInternalProcessor` | Executes cross-cutting advice (UoW, policy, JMX, tracing) before/after processor delegation |\n| `Route` / `DefaultRoute` | Runtime route; holds endpoint, consumer, processor chain, policies, configuration |\n| `RouteDefinition` | Design-time DSL model; holds from/to definitions and all EIP step definitions |\n| `RouteReifier` | Converts RouteDefinition \u2192 runtime Route + RoutePipeline + CamelInternalProcessor |\n| `ProcessorReifier` | Converts individual ProcessorDefinition \u2192 Processor, wrapped in Channel |\n| `SendReifier` / `SendProcessor` | Converts `to()` DSL to a processor that delegates to the destination's Producer |\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\nThe complete message routing flow through Apache Camel is:\n\n```\nExternal Source\n    \u2193\nConsumer (receives message, creates Exchange)\n    \u2193\nCamelInternalProcessor [route-level UoW wrapper]\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 before: UnitOfWork, RoutePolicy, InflightRepository, JMX, Lifecycle\n  \u2193\nRoutePipeline (iterates through processor list)\n  \u2193\n  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n The Processor passed is the entire route processing chain (CamelInternalProcessor wrapping RoutePipeline).\n- **Endpoint \u2194 Producer**: Endpoint creates Producer via `createProducer()` or `createAsyncProducer()`. Producer implements `Processor` so it can be used in the pipeline.\n- **Consumer \u2194 Processor chain**: Consumer calls `getAsyncProcessor().process(exchange, callback)` to push the exchange into the route's processor chain.\n- **Pipeline \u2194 Channel**: Pipeline holds a list of `AsyncProcessor` references (which are `DefaultChannel` instances). It calls each sequentially, using the reactive executor for scheduling.\n- **Channel \u2194 ErrorHandler \u2194 Processor**: Channel wraps the actual processor in an error handler (when `inheritErrorHandler` is true). The channel's `getOutput()` returns the error handler if present, otherwise the raw processor.\n- **ProcessorReifier \u2194 ProcessorDefinition**: Each concrete reifier converts its corresponding definition to a runtime Processor, then `wrapChannel()` wraps it in a DefaultChannel with interceptors.\n- **RouteReifier \u2194 RouteDefinition**: RouteReifier resolves endpoints, iterates output definitions, delegates to per-EIP reifiers, assembles the RoutePipeline, wraps with CamelInternalProcessor, and sets the result on DefaultRoute.\n\n## Summary\n\nApache Camel's message routing architecture follows a layered Abstract Factory pattern where **Component** creates **Endpoint**, which creates **Consumer** (inbound) and **Producer** (outbound), with **Processor** as the universal processing contract. The **RouteReifier** bridges the design-time DSL model (`RouteDefinition` with its `ProcessorDefinition` outputs) to the runtime by recursively converting each definition into a **Processor** wrapped in a **DefaultChannel** (which decorates it with interceptors, error handlers, and cross-cutting advice via `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice`), then assembling these channels into a **RoutePipeline** that chains them sequentially using a reactive execution model. At runtime, the Consumer receives messages, pushes them through a **CamelInternalProcessor** (handling UnitOfWork, route policies, JMX, and tracing) into the RoutePipeline, which iterates each Channel-wrapped processor step until reaching a terminal **SendProcessor** that delegates to the destination Endpoint's **Producer**.\n",

holds a reference to the processing Processor\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Producer.java` \u2014 Sends message exchanges to an Endpoint; extends both Processor and Service\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Processor.java` \u2014 Core @FunctionalInterface for processing Exchange instances; single method `process(Exchange)`\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Channel.java` \u2014 Routes exchanges between processors in the route graph; wraps processors with interceptors and error handlers\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Route.java` \u2014 Runtime route interface defining lifecycle, configuration, policies, and consumer/processor access\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/spi/InternalProcessor.java` \u2014 Internal processor API for cross-cutting concerns (UoW, tracing, debugging, JMX, route policies)\n- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/spi/CamelInternalProcessorAdvice.java` \u2014 Before/after advice interface for cross-cutting functionality in the routing engine\n\n### Base/Support Implementations (core/camel-support)\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultComponent.java` \u2014 Abstract base Component; implements URI parsing, parameter extraction, endpoint creation/configuration lifecycle\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultEndpoint.java` \u2014 Abstract base Endpoint; manages exchange creation, consumer/producer factory methods, polling consumer setup\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultConsumer.java` \u2014 Default Consumer implementation; delegates exchange creation to endpoint\n- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultAsyncProducer.java` \u2014 Async-capable Producer; bridges sync process() to async via AsyncProcessorAwaitManager\n\n### Processor Chain (core/camel-core-processor)\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/Pipeline.java` \u2014 Chains processors sequentially; output of one becomes input to the next via PipelineTask/ReactiveExecutor\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/RoutePipeline.java` \u2014 Subclass of Pipeline used as the starting point for a Route\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/PipelineHelper.java` \u2014 Decides whether to continue processing based on exchange failure/rollback/stop state\n- `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/SendProcessor.java` \u2014 Terminal processor that forwards an exchange to a destination Endpoint via its Producer\n\n### Engine (core/camel-base-engine)\n- `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultRoute.java` \u2014 Default Route implementation; creates Consumer from Endpoint.createConsumer(processor), manages services lifecycle\n- `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultChannel.java` \u2014 Default Channel implementation (extends CamelInternalProcessor); wires interceptors, error handlers, debugger, tracer, and JMX instrumentation around each processor node\n- `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java` \u2014 Core internal processor executing CamelInternalProcessorAdvice before/after callbacks for UoW, route policy, inflight tracking, tracing, debugging, stream caching, message history\n\n### Model (core/camel-core-model)\n- `core/camel-core-model/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/model/RouteDefinition.java` \u2014 DSL model class for a route; holds FromDefinition (input), outputs (processor definitions), error handler, route policies, and configuration\n\n### Reifiers (core/camel-core-reifier)\n- `core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/RouteReifier.java` \u2014 Bridges RouteDefinition model to runtime Route; resolves endpoints, creates RoutePipeline, wraps with CamelInternalProcessor/UoW, configures route policies and advices\n- `core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/ProcessorReifier.java` \u2014 Abstract base reifier; converts ProcessorDefinition to Processor, wraps each in a Channel with interceptors and error handlers, builds composite Pipeline from outputs\n- `core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/SendReifier.java` \u2014 Converts ToDefinition to SendProcessor; resolves the destination Endpoint\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### Phase 1: Route Definition (Design Time / DSL)\n1. Entry point: `core/camel-core-model/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/model/RouteDefinition.java`\n   - User defines a route via Java DSL (`from(\"timer:tick\").to(\"log:out\")`) or XML\n   - `RouteDefinition` holds a `FromDefinition` (input endpoint) and a list of `ProcessorDefinition` outputs (each EIP step)\n\n### Phase 2: Route Reification (Startup / Model\u2192Runtime Bridge)\n2. `RouteReifier.createRoute()` \u2192 `doCreateRoute()`\n   (`core/camel-core-reifier/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/reifier/RouteReifier.java`)\n   - Resolves the input `Endpoint` from the `FromDefinition`'s URI via `resolveEndpoint()`\n   - Creates a `DefaultRoute` via `PluginHelper.getRouteFactory()` with the resolved endpoint\n   - Configures route-level settings: error handler factory, tracing, message history, stream caching, delayer, auto-startup, shutdown policy\n\n3. For each output `ProcessorDefinition` in `RouteDefinition.getOutputs()`:\n   - `ProcessorReifier.reifier(route, output)` selects the appropriate reifier (e.g., `SendReifier` for `ToDefinition`)\n   - `reifier.addRoutes()` is called, which invokes `makeProcessor()`:\n     a. `createProcessor()` \u2014 calls the specific reifier's implementation (e.g., `SendReifier.createProcessor()` creates a `SendProcessor`)\n     b. `wrapProcessor(processor)` \u2192 `wrapChannel(processor, child)`:\n        - Creates a `DefaultChannel` via `PluginHelper.getInternalProcessorFactory().createChannel()`\n        - Collects interceptor strategies from: CamelContext \u2192 Route \u2192 Definition\n        - Calls `channel.initChannel()` which wires: JMX instrumentation, tracer, debugger, backlog tracer, message history advices\n        - Optionally wraps the channel output in an error handler via `wrapChannelInErrorHandler()`\n        - Calls `channel.postInitChannel()` to finalize wiring\n     c. The wrapped `Channel` is added to `route.getEventDrivenProcessors()`\n\n4. RouteReifier assembles the list of event-driven processors into a `RoutePipeline`\n   (`core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/RoutePipeline.java`)\n\n5. RouteReifier wraps the `RoutePipeline` in a `CamelInternalProcessor` with UnitOfWork advice:\n   - `PluginHelper.getInternalProcessorFactory().addUnitOfWorkProcessorAdvice(camelContext, target, route)`\n   - Adds route policy advice, inflight repository advice, JMX management advice, route lifecycle advice\n   - Adds REST binding advice, contract advice, variable advice as applicable\n   - Sets this `InternalProcessor` as `route.setProcessor(internal)`\n\n### Phase 3: Route Startup (Runtime)\n6. `DefaultRoute.gatherRootServices()` \u2192 `endpoint.createConsumer(processor)`\n   (`core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultRoute.java:685`)\n   - The route's endpoint creates a `Consumer` passing the route's processor (the `CamelInternalProcessor` wrapping the `RoutePipeline`)\n   - The consumer is started as part of the route's service lifecycle\n\n### Phase 4: Message Processing (Runtime)\n7. Consumer receives a message from the external source (e.g., timer fires, HTTP request arrives):\n   - `DefaultConsumer.createExchange(autoRelease)` creates a new `Exchange` from the `ExchangeFactory`\n   - Consumer calls `getAsyncProcessor().process(exchange, callback)` \u2014 this invokes the route's processor chain\n\n8. `CamelInternalProcessor.process(exchange, callback)` (top-level UoW wrapper):\n   (`core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java:285`)\n   - Executes all `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice.before(exchange)` in order:\n     - UnitOfWork creation/tracking\n     - Route policy `onExchangeBegin()`\n     - Inflight repository increment\n     - JMX instrumentation start\n     - Message history recording\n     - Stream caching\n   - Delegates to `processor.process(exchange, asyncCallback)` \u2014 the wrapped `RoutePipeline`\n   - After completion, executes all advices' `after(exchange, state)` in reverse order\n\n9. `Pipeline.process(exchange, callback)` (the RoutePipeline):\n   (`core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/Pipeline.java`)\n   - Acquires a `PipelineTask` from the task factory\n   - Schedules the task on the `ReactiveExecutor`\n   - `PipelineTask.run()` iterates through the processor list:\n     a. Calls `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn(exchange)` to copy OUT\u2192IN for the next step\n     b. Calls `PipelineHelper.continueProcessing(exchange)` to check for errors/stop/rollback\n     c. Gets the next `AsyncProcessor` (which is a `DefaultChannel` wrapping the actual EIP processor)\n     d. Calls `processor.process(exchange, this)` where `this` (PipelineTask) is the callback\n     e. On callback `done()`, re-schedules itself via `ReactiveExecutor` to process the next step\n     f. When all processors are exhausted, calls `ExchangeHelper.copyResults()` and signals the original callback\n\n10. `DefaultChannel.process(exchange, callback)` (each EIP step):\n    (`core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultChannel.java`)\n    - DefaultChannel extends `CamelInternalProcessor`, so it follows the same advice pattern:\n      - Executes per-node advices: message history, debugger, backlog tracer, JMX instrumentation\n      - Delegates to its output \u2014 which is either the error handler wrapping the next processor, or the next processor directly\n    - The error handler intercepts exceptions and applies redelivery/dead-letter-channel policies\n\n11. At a `to(\"...\")` step, the `SendProcessor.process(exchange, callback)` is invoked:\n    (`core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/SendProcessor.java`)\n    - Resolves and caches the destination's `AsyncProducer`\n    - Calls `producer.process(exchange, callback)` to deliver the exchange to the destination endpoint\n    - Restores the original exchange pattern after send\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Abstract Factory Pattern**: `Component` \u2192 `Endpoint` \u2192 `Consumer`/`Producer`. Each Component is a factory for Endpoints, and each Endpoint is a factory for Consumers and Producers. This three-level factory hierarchy enables pluggable transport/protocol support.\n\n2. **Pipes and Filters (Pipeline) Pattern**: The `Pipeline` processor implements the classic Pipes and Filters EIP. Each processor in the pipeline receives the output of the previous processor as its input. The `PipelineTask` manages sequential execution through the processor chain using a reactive callback model.\n\n3. **Chain of Responsibility Pattern**: The `Channel` (DefaultChannel) wraps each processor node with interceptors and error handlers, forming a chain of responsibility. Interceptor strategies are collected from three scopes: CamelContext-global, route-level, and definition-level.\n\n4. **Interceptor / Advice Pattern**: `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice` implements the before/after advice pattern for cross-cutting concerns. Multiple advices are composed into the `CamelInternalProcessor` and executed in sorted order (via `Ordered`), with `after()` callbacks running in reverse order. This replaces what would otherwise be deeply nested processor wrappers, reducing stack depth.\n\n5. **Bridge Pattern (Reifier)**: The `ProcessorReifier` hierarchy bridges the model layer (design-time DSL definitions) to the runtime layer (executable processors). Each `ProcessorDefinition` subclass has a corresponding `ProcessorReifier` that knows how to create the runtime processor. `RouteReifier` orchestrates this for the entire route.\n\n6. **Template Method Pattern**: `DefaultComponent.createEndpoint(String uri)` implements the template method \u2014 it handles URI parsing, parameter extraction, and property binding, then delegates to the abstract `createEndpoint(String uri, String remaining, Map<String, Object> parameters)` which concrete components override.\n\n7. **Decorator Pattern**: The `DefaultChannel` decorates the actual processor with error handling, interceptors, debugging, tracing, and JMX instrumentation. The `CamelInternalProcessor` at the route level decorates the entire `RoutePipeline` with UnitOfWork, route policy, and inflight tracking.\n\n8. **Object Pool Pattern**: Both `Pipeline` and `CamelInternalProcessor` use `PooledExchangeTaskFactory` and `PooledObjectFactory` respectively to reuse task objects, reducing GC pressure in high-throughput scenarios.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|-----------|---------------|\n| `Component` | URI-based factory for Endpoints; handles component-level configuration |\n| `Endpoint` | Factory for Consumers and Producers; defines exchange pattern; provides exchange creation |\n| `Consumer` | Receives messages from external source; creates Exchange; delegates to processor chain |\n| `Producer` | Sends Exchange to external destination; implements Processor interface |\n| `Processor` | Core processing unit; single `process(Exchange)` method |\n| `Pipeline` / `RoutePipeline` | Chains processors sequentially using reactive execution model |\n| `Channel` / `DefaultChannel` | Wraps individual processors with interceptors, error handlers, tracing, debugging |\n| `CamelInternalProcessor` | Executes cross-cutting advice (UoW, policy, JMX, tracing) before/after processor delegation |\n| `Route` / `DefaultRoute` | Runtime route; holds endpoint, consumer, processor chain, policies, configuration |\n| `RouteDefinition` | Design-time DSL model; holds from/to definitions and all EIP step definitions |\n| `RouteReifier` | Converts RouteDefinition \u2192 runtime Route + RoutePipeline + CamelInternalProcessor |\n| `ProcessorReifier` | Converts individual ProcessorDefinition \u2192 Processor, wrapped in Channel |\n| `SendReifier` / `SendProcessor` | Converts `to()` DSL to a processor that delegates to the destination's Producer |\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\nThe complete message routing flow through Apache Camel is:\n\n```\nExternal Source\n    \u2193\nConsumer (receives message, creates Exchange)\n    \u2193\nCamelInternalProcessor [route-level UoW wrapper]\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 before: UnitOfWork, RoutePolicy, InflightRepository, JMX, Lifecycle\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n  \u2502 For each EIP step:                           \u2502\n  \u2502                                              \u2502\n  \u2502  DefaultChannel [per-node CamelInternalProc] \u2502\n  \u2502    \u251c\u2500\u2500 before: MessageHistory, Debugger,     \u2502\n  \u2502    \u2502          BacklogTracer, JMX             \u2502\n  \u2502    \u2193                                         \u2502\n  \u2502  ErrorHandler (optional, wraps output)       \u2502\n  \u2502    \u2193                                         \u2502\n  \u2502  Actual Processor (e.g., filter, transform)  \u2502\n  \u2502    \u2193                                         \u2502\n  \u2502  DefaultChannel.after: reverse advices       \u2502\n  \u2502                                              \u2502\n  \u2502  ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn(exchange)     \u2502\n  \u2502  PipelineHelper.continueProcessing(exchange) \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n    \u2193 (repeat for each processor in pipeline)\n\n  Final step often: SendProcessor\n    \u2193\n  Producer.process(exchange) \u2192 destination Endpoint\n    \u2193\nCamelInternalProcessor # Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture

## Files Examined

### API Interfaces (core/camel-api)
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Component.java` — Factory interface for creating Endpoint instances from URIs; extends CamelContextAware, Service
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Endpoint.java` — Message Endpoint pattern interface; factory for Producer, Consumer, and Exchange instances
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Consumer.java` — Consumes message exchanges from an Endpoint; holds a reference to the processing Processor
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Producer.java` — Sends message exchanges to an Endpoint; extends both Processor and Service
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Processor.java` — Core @FunctionalInterface for processing Exchange instances; single method `process(Exchange)`
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Channel.java` — Routes exchanges between processors in the route graph; wraps processors with interceptors and error handlers
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Route.java` — Runtime route interface defining lifecycle, configuration, policies, and consumer/processor access
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/spi/InternalProcessor.java` — Internal processor API for cross-cutting concerns (UoW, tracing, debugging, JMX, route policies)
- `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/spi/CamelInternalProcessorAdvice.java` — Before/after advice interface for cross-cutting functionality in the routing engine

- `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultComponent.java` — Abstract base Component; implements URI parsing, parameter extraction, endpoint creation/con
... (truncated)
